                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Liquid Phase Exfoliated MoS2 Nanosheets Percolated with Carbon Nanotubes for High Volumetric/Areal Capacity Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuping; He, Xiaoyun; Hanlon, Damien; Harvey, Andrew; Coleman, Jonathan N.; Li, Yanguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8821-8828</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The search for high-capacity, low-cost electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries is a significant challenge in energy research.  Among the many potential candidates, layered compds. such as MoS2 have attracted increasing attention.  However, such materials have not yet fulfilled their true potential.  Here, we show that networks of liq. phase exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets, reinforced with 20 wt % single-wall carbon nanotubes (SWNTs), can be formed into sodium-ion battery electrodes with large gravimetric, volumetric, and areal capacity.  The MoS2/SWNT composite films are highly porous, elec. conductive, and mech. robust due to its percolating carbon nanotube network.  When directly employed as the working electrode, they exhibit a specific capacity of &gt;400 mAh/g and volumetric capacity of ∼650 mAh/cm3.  Their mech. stability allows them to be processed into free-standing films with tunable thickness up to ∼100 μm, corresponding to an areal loading of 15 mg/cm2.  Their high elec. cond. allows the high volumetric capacity to be retained, even at high thickness, resulting in state-of-the-art areal capacities of &gt;4.0 mAh/cm2.  Such values are competitive with their lithium-ion counterparts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGptS6q-a8cmzrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgAFHuL5G9TQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtlOqu73E&amp;md5=79d9c657488cc05fe8a5e0f8dae21b9d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201800641"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous Co0.85Se@reduced graphene oxide ultrathin nanosheets with vacancy-enhanced kinetics as superior anodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Yongxin; Wang, Ziheng; Jiang, Ying; Li, Shuaijie; Li, Zehua; Zhang, Haiqin; Wu, Feng; Xie, Man; Li, Li; Chen, Renjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal selenides have received much attention from the rechargeable battery community owing to their considerable capacity.  However, attainment of a long cycle life and fast Na+ storage kinetics are still needed to enable their practical application.  Co0.85Se nanosheets prepd. using a simple hydrothermal method exhibit a hierarchical porous structure, which is conducive to fast electrolyte transport and rapid adsorption of Na+ ions.  Herein, to improve the electronic cond. of Co0.85Se, reduced graphene oxide (rGO) is introduced to construct a three-dimensional network and achieve fast electronic transport.  This defect-controlled Co0.85Se@rGO anode exhibits a highly reversible capacity of 460 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1.  Outstanding durability and remarkable rate stability are also achieved via the synergistic effects of vacancy transport and the heterostructure between Co0.85Se and rGO.  Furthermore, the Na+ insertion/extn. mechanism is systematically investigated using ex situ X-ray diffraction, Raman spectroscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and a series of electrochem. analyses.  These analyses enable detailed characterization of the ionic diffusion kinetics and corresponding components and structural changes.  Finally, a first-principles approach is employed to det. the diffusion energy barrier of Na+ ions in perfect CoSe and defective Co0.85Se.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpnYZxWikZ_RLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgjUXPNHh_HFg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhslejsbnN&amp;md5=ec261ec0e0b14c55713e3f8e100011d8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201308354"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The chemistry of two-dimensional layered transition metal dichalcogenide nanosheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chhowalla Manish; Shin Hyeon Suk; Eda Goki; Li Lain-Jong; Loh Kian Ping; Zhang Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">263-75</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Ultrathin two-dimensional nanosheets of layered transition metal dichalcogenides (TMDs) are fundamentally and technologically intriguing.  In contrast to the graphene sheet, they are chemically versatile.  Mono- or few-layered TMDs - obtained either through exfoliation of bulk materials or bottom-up syntheses - are direct-gap semiconductors whose bandgap energy, as well as carrier type (n- or p-type), varies between compounds depending on their composition, structure and dimensionality.  In this Review, we describe how the tunable electronic structure of TMDs makes them attractive for a variety of applications.  They have been investigated as chemically active electrocatalysts for hydrogen evolution and hydrosulfurization, as well as electrically active materials in opto-electronics.  Their morphologies and properties are also useful for energy storage applications such as electrodes for Li-ion batteries and supercapacitors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTRX3K9n3xrikBuFdjgVNKSfW6udTcc2eb0MNewLT5UU7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pure and stable metallic phase molybdenum disulfide nanosheets for hydrogen evolution reaction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Geng, Xiumei; Sun, Weiwei; Wu, Wei; Chen, Benjamin; Al-Hilo, Alaa; Benamara, Mourad; Zhu, Hongli; Watanabe, Fumiya; Cui, Jingbiao; Chen, Tar-pin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic-phase MoS2 (M-MoS2) is metastable and does not exist in nature.  Pure and stable M-MoS2 has not been previously prepd. by chem. synthesis, to the best of our knowledge.  Here we report a hydrothermal process for synthesizing stable two-dimensional M-MoS2 nanosheets in water.  The metal-metal Raman stretching mode at 146 cm-1 in the M-MoS2 structure, as predicted by theor. calcns., is exptl. obsd.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical vapor deposited MoS2/electrospun carbon nanofiber composite as anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chen; Li, Guoqing; Lu, Yao; Zhu, Jiadeng; Jiang, Mengjin; Hu, Yi; Cao, Linyou; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to its high theor. capacity and unique layered structure, MoS2 has attracted attention as a Na-ion battery anode material.  However, the electrochem. performance of MoS2 based anodes is hindered by their low intrinsic cond. and large vol. change during cycling.  Nano-sized MoS2 sheets were synthesized using a scalable CVD method on the surface of electrospun C nanofibers (CNFs).  The morphol. of the resultant MoS2@CNFs was studied by SEM, TEM and x-ray diffraction, while their electrochem. performance was studied using cyclic voltammetry and galvanostatic charge-discharge.  A strong interconnection between MoS2 nanosheets and CNFs is formed and the conductive network of CNFs is beneficial for the Na ion kinetics.  When studied as an anode for Na-ion batteries, a high reversible capacity of 380 mA h g-1 was obtained after 50 cycles with good cycling stability.  In particular, MoS2@CNFs can deliver a capacity of 198 mA h g-1 under a high c.d. of 1 A g-1 after 500 cycles, indicating their great potential as anode material for long-life Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpINaOxNvKXNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgS9PaHHDri_A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvF2gu7vF&amp;md5=1125a03e3dca583bd705f6da2fb4f1c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201300415"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, J.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-Like MoS2/Graphene Composites: Cationic Surfactant-Assisted Hydrothermal Synthesis and Electrochemical Reversible Storage of Lithium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Guochuang; Chen, Tao; Chen, Weixiang; Wang, Zhen; Chang, Kun; Ma, Lin; Huang, Feihe; Chen, Dongyun; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A cationic surfactant-assisted hydrothermal route is developed for the facile synthesis of graphene-like MoS2/graphene (GL-MoS2/G) composites based on the hydrothermal redn. of Na2MoO4 and graphene oxide sheets with L-cysteine in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB), following by annealing in N2 atmosphere.  The GL-MoS2/G composites are characterized by X-ray diffraction, electron microscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and Raman spectroscopy.  The effects of CTAB concn. on the microstructures and electrochem. performances of the composites for reversible Li+ storage are investigated.  It is found that the layer no. of MoS2 sheets decreases with increasing CTAB concn.  The GL-MoS2 sheets in the composites are few-layer in the case of 0.01∼0.03 mol L-1 CTAB of hydrothermal soln. and single-layer in the case of 0.05 mol L-1 CTAB.  The GL-MoS2/G composites prepd. with 0.01-0.02 mol·L-1 of CTAB soln. exhibit a higher reversible capacity of 940-1020 mAh g-1, a greater cycle stability, and a higher rate capability than other samples.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Single-Layered Ultrasmall Nanoplates of MoS2 Embedded in Carbon Nanofibers with Excellent Electrochemical Performance for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Mu, Xiaoke; van Aken, Peter A.; Yu, Yan; Maier, Joachim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The prepn. and electrochem. storage behavior of MoS2 nanodots-more precisely single-layered ultrasmall nanoplates-embedded in C nanowires was studied.  The prepn. is achieved by an electrospinning process that can be easily scaled up.  The rate performance and cycling stability of both Li and Na storage are outstanding.  The storage behavior is, also, highly exciting from a fundamental point of view, as the differences between the usual storage modes-insertion, conversion, interfacial storage-are beneficially blurred.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Petal-like MoS2 Nanosheets Space-Confined in Hollow Mesoporous Carbon Spheres for Enhanced Lithium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xiue; Zhao, Rongfang; Wu, Qianhui; Li, Wenlong; Shen, Chao; Ni, Lubin; Yan, Hui; Diao, Guowang; Chen, Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">An innovative approach for efficient synthesis of petal-like molybdenum disulfide nanosheets inside hollow mesoporous carbon spheres (HMCSs), the yolk-shell structured MoS2@C, has been developed.  HMCSs effectively control and confine in situ growth of MoS2 nanosheets and significantly improve the cond. and structural stability of the hybrid material.  The yolk-shell structured MoS2@C is proven to achieve high reversible capacity (993 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 200 cycles), superior rate capability (595 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 10 A g-1), and excellent cycle performance (962 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 1000 cycles and 624 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1 after 400 cycles) when evaluated as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries.  This superior performance is attributed to the yolk-shell structure with conductive mesoporous carbon as the shell and the stack of two-dimensional MoS2 nanosheets as the yolk.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpjEXGjpcOjxLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilBkMd6eHtPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1elurjO&amp;md5=f41f073a0a5a945dd6c9c6108fb03c0e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201401521"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Langrock, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mignerey, A.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced MoS2/Carbon Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Gao, Tao; Langrock, Alex; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">473-481</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcL7gViWJlhrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilBkMd6eHtPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOitbg%253D&amp;md5=6ec4e5e6db41f69f19d690e591e04ffa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA00114A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Khawula, T. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sigalas, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ozoemena, K.                 10.1039/C6TA00114A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D6411-6425%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DT.%2BN.%2BY.%2BKhawula%26author%3DK.%2BRaju%26author%3DP.%2BJ.%2BFranklyn%26author%3DI.%2BSigalas%26author%3DK.%2BI.%2BOzoemena%26title%3DSymmetric%2BPseudocapacitors%2Bbased%2Bon%2BMolybdenum%2BDisulfide%2B%2528MoS2%2529-Modified%2BCarbon%2BNanospheres%253A%2BCorrelating%2BPhysicochemistry%2Band%2BSynergistic%2BInteraction%2Bon%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC6TA00114A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b04260&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC6TA00114A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Symmetric pseudocapacitors based on molybdenum disulfide (MoS2)-modified carbon nanospheres: correlating physicochemistry and synergistic interaction on energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Khawula, Tobile N. Y.; Raju, Kumar; Franklyn, Paul J.; Sigalas, Iakovos; Ozoemena, Kenneth I.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6411-6425</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide-modified carbon nanospheres (MoS2/CNS) with two different morphologies (spherical and flower-like) were synthesized using hydrothermal techniques and studied as sym. pseudocapacitors in an aq. electrolyte.  The physicochem. properties of these MoS2/CNS layered materials were studied using surface area anal. (BET), SEM, TEM, XRD, Raman, FTIR spectroscopy, and advanced electrochem., including cyclic voltammetry (CV), galvanostatic cycling with potential limitation (GCPL), long-hour voltage-holding tests, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS).  The two different MoS2/CNS layered materials exhibit unique differences in morphol., surface area, and structural parameters, which were correlated with their electrochem. capacitive properties.  The flower-like morphol. (f-MoS2/CNS) shows lattice expansion (XRD), large surface area (BET anal.), and small-sized nanostructures (corroborated by the larger FWHM of the Raman and XRD data).  In contrast to the f-MoS2/CNS, the spherical morphol. (s-MoS2/CNS) shows lattice contraction and small surface area with relatively large-sized nanostructures.  The presence of CNS on the MoS2 structure leads to slight softening of the characteristic Raman bands (E12g and A1g modes) with larger FWHM.  MoS2 and its CNS-based composites were tested in sym. electrochem. capacitors in an aq. 1 M Na2SO4 soln.  CNS improves the cond. of the MoS2 and synergistically enhances the electrochem. capacitive properties of the materials, esp. the f-MoS2/CNS-based sym. cells (most notably, in terms of capacitance retention).  The f-MoS2/CNS-based pseudocapacitor shows a max. capacitance of 231 F/g, with high energy d. 26 W-h/kg and power d. 6443 W/kg.  For the s-MoS2/CNS-based pseudocapacitor, the equiv. values are 108 F/g, 7.4 W-h/kg and 3700 W/kg.  The high-performance of the f-MoS2/CNS is consistent with its physicochem. properties as detd. by the spectroscopy and microscopy data.  These findings have opened doors for further exploration of the synergistic effects between MoS2 graphene-like sheets and CNS for energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosWmg3JgAFB7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilBkMd6eHtPw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XkvVCnurc%253D&amp;md5=c542786281bca67dd9222055311a3f05</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/nn200659w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">L-Cysteine-Assisted Synthesis of Layered MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composites with Excellent Electrochemical Performances for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4720</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4728</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/nn200659w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D4720-4728%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DK.%2BChang%26author%3DW.%2BChen%26title%3DL-Cysteine-Assisted%2BSynthesis%2Bof%2BLayered%2BMoS2%252FGraphene%2BComposites%2Bwith%2BExcellent%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformances%2Bfor%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fnn200659w&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b04260&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fnn200659w&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">L-Cysteine-Assisted Synthesis of Layered MoS2/Graphene Composites with Excellent Electrochemical Performances for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chang, Kun; Chen, Weixiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4720-4728</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile process was developed to synthesize layered MoS2/graphene (MoS2/G) composites by an L-cysteine-assisted soln.-phase method, in which sodium molybdate, as-prepd. graphene oxide (GO), and L-cysteine were used as starting materials.  As-prepd. MoS2/G was then fabricated into layered MoS2/G composites after annealing in a H2/N2 atmosphere at 800° for 2 h.  The samples were systematically studied by x-ray diffraction, field emission SEM, energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy, and high-resoln. TEM.  Electrochem. performances were evaluated in two-electrode cells vs. metallic lithium.  The obtained MoS2/G composites show three-dimensional architecture and excellent electrochem. performances as anode materials for Li-ion batteries.  The MoS2/G composite with a Mo:C molar ratio of 1:2 exhibits the highest specific capacity of ∼1100 mAh/g at a current of 100 mA/g, as well as excellent cycling stability and high-rate capability.  The superior electrochem. performances of MoS2/G composites as Li-ion battery anodes are attributed to their robust composite structure and the synergistic effects between layered MoS2 and graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCZ2OkL_eUGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljw1pPVLx9KgQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXmtlyms7c%253D&amp;md5=1ab1063ee9a071ae41ed3a39f457ff97</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/nn406156b"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">David, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bhandavat, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1759</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1770</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">David, Lamuel; Bhandavat, Romil; Singh, Gurpreet</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We study the synthesis and electrochem. and mech. performance of layered free-standing papers composed of acid-exfoliated few-layer molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) flakes for use as a self-standing flexible electrode in sodium-ion batteries.  Synthesis was achieved through vacuum filtration of homogeneous dispersions consisting of varying wt. percent of acid-treated MoS2 flakes in GO in DI water, followed by thermal redn. at elevated temps.  The electrochem. performance of the crumpled composite paper (at 4 mg.cm-2) was evaluated as counter electrode against pure Na foil in a half-cell configuration.  The electrode showed good Na cycling ability with a stable charge capacity of ∼230 mAh.g-1 with respect to total wt. of the electrode with Coulombic efficiency reaching ∼99%.  In addn., static uniaxial tensile tests performed on crumpled composite papers showed high av. strain to failure reaching ∼2%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqX-na1eCQtCLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljw1pPVLx9KgQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpslejsw%253D%253D&amp;md5=d45da3902a48ed0a91ed1278d69862fb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.04.032"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene-Based Nano-Materials for Lithium–Sulfur Battery and Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">379</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">405</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-based nano-materials for lithium-sulfur battery and sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Songping; Ge, Rongyun; Lu, Mingjia; Xu, Rui; Zhang, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene-based nano-materials have provided an opportunity for next-generation energy storage device, particularly for lithium-sulfur battery and sodium-ion battery (SIB), due to their unique properties.  This review comprehensively summarizes the present achievements and the latest progress of inorg. nano-materials/graphene composites as the electrode materials for Li-S battery and SIBs.  Electrochem. principles, performances and key obstructions of graphene-based materials in the actual application are considered.  This review gathers and classifies updated knowledge about Li-S battery and SIB nanomaterials related to graphene, with the aim of offering a wide view of those systems.  It is concluded that cost-effective SIBs and Li-S battery are promising next-generation battery candidates in the near future, but require further investigation and improvement to deal with some crit. scientific issues.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGquh6fB9vQzeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljw1pPVLx9KgQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXos1egtb4%253D&amp;md5=ba9ca7c744e220be6630dcb28320c4e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms3922"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, D.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-capacity antimony sulphide nanoparticle-decorated graphene composite as anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu Denis Y W; Prikhodchenko Petr V; Mason Chad W; Batabyal Sudip K; Gun Jenny; Sladkevich Sergey; Medvedev Alexander G; Lev Ovadia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2922</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are an alternative to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale applications.  However, low capacity and poor rate capability of existing anodes are the main bottlenecks to future developments.  Here we report a uniform coating of antimony sulphide (stibnite) on graphene, fabricated by a solution-based synthesis technique, as the anode material for sodium-ion batteries.  It gives a high capacity of 730 mAh g(-1) at 50 mA g(-1), an excellent rate capability up to 6C and a good cycle performance.  The promising performance is attributed to fast sodium ion diffusion from the small nanoparticles, and good electrical transport from the intimate contact between the active material and graphene, which also provides a template for anchoring the nanoparticles.  We also demonstrate a battery with the stibnite-graphene composite that is free from sodium metal, having energy density up to 80 Wh kg(-1).  The energy density could exceed that of some lithium-ion batteries with further optimization.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQGZMXlr7vNCe3MPKNEWB5RfW6udTcc2eYEX6RR_k0YH7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2c3ltFajuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=00d6ac79468675541d9951b7cfb704e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1038/nmat4170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Raccichini, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Varzi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Passerini, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Scrosati, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Role of Graphene for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">An improved method for the prepn. of graphene oxide (GO) is described.  Currently, Hummers' method (KMnO4, NaNO3, H2SO4) is the most common method used for prepg. graphene oxide.  We have found that excluding the NaNO3, increasing the amt. of KMnO4, and performing the reaction in a 9:1 mixt. of H2SO4/H3PO4 improves the efficiency of the oxidn. process.  This improved method provides a greater amt. of hydrophilic oxidized graphene material as compared to Hummers' method or Hummers' method with addnl. KMnO4.  Moreover, even though the GO produced by our method is more oxidized than that prepd. by Hummers' method, when both are reduced in the same chamber with hydrazine, chem. converted graphene (CCG) produced from this new method is equiv. in its elec. cond.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  One of the main issues in the prodn. of polymer nanocomposites is the dispersion state of filler as multilayered graphene (MLG) and carbon nanotubes (CNTs) tend to agglomerate due to van der Waals forces.  The agglomeration can be avoided by using org. solvents, selecting suitable dispersion and prodn. methods, and functionalizing the fillers.  Another proposed method is the use of hybrid fillers as synergistic effects can cause an improvement in the dispersion state of the fillers.  In this review article, various aspects of each process that can help avoid filler agglomeration and improve dispersion state are discussed in detail.  This review article would be helpful for both current and prospective researchers in the field of MLG- and CNT-based polymer nanocomposites to achieve max. enhancement in mech., thermal, and elec. properties of produced polymer nanocomposites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWneFE-OXIlLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXHzFv1ggKPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslyqsbjE&amp;md5=80747645c9c85b2401d8a00944ab6d36</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/ar300180n"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Material Processing of Chemically Modified Graphene: Some Challenges and Solutions</span>. <i>Acc.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Material Processing of Chemically Modified Graphene: Some Challenges and Solutions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Jiayan; Kim, Jaemyung; Huang, Jiaxing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Graphene-based sheets show promise for a variety of potential applications, and researchers in many scientific disciplines are interested in these materials.  Although researchers have developed many ways of generating single at. layer carbon sheets, chem. exfoliation of graphite powders to graphene oxide (GO) sheets followed by deoxygenation to form chem. modified graphene (CMG) offers a promising route for bulk scale prodn.  The materials processing, which we broadly define as the phys. and chem. means to tailor a material's chem. and microstructures, enables us to control the properties in bulk CMG materials.  For example, by processing CMG sheets in different solvents, we can make thin films, blend CMG sheets with other materials, and modify them by chem. reactions.  Materials processing methods also allow us to control the interactions between CMG sheets for the assembly of large scale two- or three-dimensional structures with desirable microstructures.  This Account highlights a few problems assocd. with large scale prodn. and processing of GO and CMG.  First, we briefly discuss the potential fire risk of GO and CMG when alk. salt byproducts are not completely removed.  These impurities can catalyze carbon combustion.  We introduce an improved purifn. procedure that effectively removes the byproducts and speeds up the prodn.  Next, we address the challenges of imaging GO and CMG sheets on common substrates such as glass and plastics using std. microscopy methods.  We have introduced a new technique fluorescence quenching microscopy (FQM), which allows us to observe graphene-based sheets with both high throughput and high contrast on arbitrary substrates and even in soln.  Then we focus on how to prevent aggregation in CMG.  Aggregation greatly reduces the material processability and accessible surface area, which degrades the material properties.  We introduce two strategies to reduce aggregation by (i) reducing the lateral dimension of the sheets to nanometer range to enhance their colloidal stability and (ii) crumpling the sheets into paper ball-like, fractal-dimensional particles to make them aggregation-resistant in both solvents and solid state, even after mech. compression.  Solns. to these material processing challenges can pave the way for further research and development.  We hope that the tools and strategies presented in this Account can facilitate the processing and property control of this promising material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpiyIfOWCqeWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXHzFv1ggKPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXivVyis7s%253D&amp;md5=f13ca0e77f8f5473f9335ef602a54b4b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1038/srep20335"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanospherical Like Reduced Graphene Oxide Decorated TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles: An Advanced Catalyst for the Hydrogen Evolution Reaction</span>. <i>Sci.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vacancy-Induced Ferromagnetism of MoS2 Nanosheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cai, Liang; He, Jingfu; Liu, Qinghua; Yao, Tao; Chen, Lin; Yan, Wensheng; Hu, Fengchun; Jiang, Yong; Zhao, Yidong; Hu, Tiandou; Sun, Zhihu; Wei, Shiqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Outstanding magnetic properties are highly desired for two-dimensional ultrathin semiconductor nanosheets.  Here, the authors propose a phase incorporation strategy to induce robust room-temp. ferromagnetism in a nonmagnetic MoS2 semiconductor.  A two-step hydrothermal method was used to intentionally introduce S vacancies in a 2H-MoS2 ultrathin nanosheet host, which prompts the transformation of the surrounding 2H-MoS2 local lattice into a trigonal (1T-MoS2) phase. 25% 1T-MoS2 phase incorporation in 2H-MoS2 nanosheets can enhance the electron carrier concn. by an order, introduce a Mo4+ 4d energy state within the bandgap, and create a robust intrinsic ferromagnetic response of 0.25 μB/Mo by the exchange interactions between S vacancy and the Mo4+ 4d bandgap state at room temp.  This design opens up new possibility for effective manipulation of exchange interactions in two-dimensional nanostructures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqWo9ethOPobVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgXHzFv1ggKPg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvV2jur0%253D&amp;md5=bc402f690787101380b37580e914b30d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201302685"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2-Based Nanocomposites for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Tianyi; Xue Huaiguo; Chen Shuangqiang; Pang Huan; Yu Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2 Nanoflowers with Expanded Interlayers as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Wang, Lixiu; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Cheng, Fangyi; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayer spacing of the (002) plane were synthesized and used as high-performance anode in Na-ion batteries.  By controlling the cut-off voltage to the range of 0.4-3 V, an intercalation mechanism rather than a conversion reaction is taking place.  The MoS2 nanoflower electrode shows high discharge capacities of 350 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, 300 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 195 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  An initial capacity increase with cycling is caused by peeling off MoS2 layers, which produces more active sites for Na+ storage.  The stripping of MoS2 layers occurring in charge/discharge cycling contributes to the enhanced kinetics and low energy barrier for the intercalation of Na+ ions.  The electrochem. reaction is mainly controlled by the capacitive process, which facilitates the high-rate capability.  Therefore, MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers hold promise for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0lywDrXEibbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljbsA_OOv5QTw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFShtL3P&amp;md5=218e207e71a96b8802293b3796174e5a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1038/srep09254"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Membranes of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Sci.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Membranes of MoS2/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Xiaoqin; Luo, Wei; Hu, Xianluo; Chen, Chaoji; Qie, Long; Hou, Dongfang; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible membrane consisting of MoS2/carbon nanofibers has been fabricated by a simple electrospinning method.  MoS2 nanosheets are uniformly encapsulated in the inter-connected carbon nanofibers with diams. of ∼150 nm.  When evaluated as a binder-free electrode for sodium-ion batteries, the as-obtained electrode demonstrates high performances, including high reversible capacity of 381.7 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and superior rate capability (283.3, 246.5 and 186.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5, 1 and 2 A g-1, resp.).                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Ni-Mo-S nanosheets on carbon fiber cloth: a flexible electrode for efficient hydrogen generation in neutral electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Miao, Jianwei; Xiao, Fang-Xing; Yang, Hong Bin; Khoo, Si Yun; Chen, Jiazang; Fan, Zhanxi; Hsu, Ying-Ya; Chen, Hao Ming; Zhang, Hua; Liu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A unique functional electrode made of hierarchal Ni-Mo-S nanosheets with abundant exposed edges anchored on conductive and flexible carbon fiber cloth, referred to as Ni-Mo-S/C, has been developed through a facile biomol.-assisted hydrothermal method.  The incorporation of Ni atoms in Mo-S plays a crucial role in tuning its intrinsic catalytic property by creating substantial defect sites as well as modifying the morphol. of Ni-Mo-S network at at. scale, resulting in an impressive enhancement in the catalytic activity.  The Ni-Mo-S/C electrode exhibits a large cathodic current and a low onset potential for hydrogen evolution reaction in neutral electrolyte (pH ∼7), for example, c.d. of 10 mA/cm2 at a very small overpotential of 200 mV.  Furthermore, the Ni-Mo-S/C electrode has excellent electrocatalytic stability over an extended period, much better than those of MoS2/C and Pt plate electrodes.  Scanning and transmission electron microscopy, Raman spectroscopy, x-ray diffraction, XPS, and x-ray absorption spectroscopy were used to understand the formation process and electrocatalytic properties of Ni-Mo-S/C.  The intuitive comparison test was designed to reveal the superior gas-evolving profile of Ni-Mo-S/C over that of MoS2/C, and a lab.-scale hydrogen generator was further assembled to demonstrate its potential application in practical appliances.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqsVDMtTB_dGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljbsA_OOv5QTw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interface Synergistic Effect from Layered Metal Sulfides of MoS2/SnS2 van der Waals Heterojunction with Enhanced Li-Ion Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Man, Xiaolei; Liang, Pei; Shu, Haibo; Zhang, Lin; Wang, Dan; Chao, Dongliang; Liu, Zugang; Du, Xiaoqing; Wan, Houzhao; Wang, Hao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered metal sulfides (LMSs) with larger interlayer spacing are suitable for Li+ intercalation/extn. and possess relatively higher theor. specific capacity than com. graphite.  However, pure LMSs show inherent low cond. and irreversible huge vol. expansion in lithium uptakes.  In this work, we introduce an interesting van der Waals heterojunction between two popular LMSs, i.e., MoS2/SnS2 van der Waals heterojunction grown on reduced graphene oxide (MoS2/SnS2-rGO), which is synthesized by a facile hydrothermal process.  The MoS2/SnS2-rGO nanocomposite exhibits a remarkable interface synergistic effect due to the weak van der Waals interaction on their nanocryst., which leads to an enhanced energy storage performance compared with MoS2-rGO and SnS2-rGO.  The MoS2/SnS2-rGO exhibits better cycling stability of 894 mAh g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 55 cycles and excellent rate performance of 590 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for LIBs.  This work proposes that weaker van der Waals interactions between the LMS can induce much more layer space for Li+ in LIBs, which might be another way to improve the storage performance of LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpQi529tYN3RbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7Mk0sVp_T-w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFerurvO&amp;md5=8538bc39f7e1cb2c18a6da13dd9ee5ab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1021/nn1003937"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brus, L.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anomalous Lattice Vibrations of Single- and Few-Layer MoS2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Changgu; Yan, Hugen; Brus, Louis E.; Heinz, Tony F.; Hone, James; Ryu, Sunmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) of single- and few-layer thickness was exfoliated on SiO2/Si substrate and characterized by Raman spectroscopy.  The no. of S-Mo-S layers of the samples was independently detd. by contact-mode at. force microscopy.  Two Raman modes, E12g and A1g, exhibited sensitive thickness dependence, with the frequency of the former decreasing and that of the latter increasing with thickness.  The results provide a convenient and reliable means for detg. layer thickness with at.-level precision.  The opposite direction of the frequency shifts, which cannot be explained solely by van der Waals interlayer coupling, is attributed to Coulombic interactions and possible stacking-induced changes of the intralayer bonding.  This work exemplifies the evolution of structural parameters in layered materials in changing from the three-dimensional to the two-dimensional regime.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVPJpIcbtgaLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7Mk0sVp_T-w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXkslKktLc%253D&amp;md5=2bf8b27f754f40e5cdf890343171555f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201703493"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, B.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quasi-Emulsion Confined Synthesis of Edge-Rich Ultrathin MoS2 Nanosheets/Graphene Hybrid for Enhanced Hydrogen Evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Xuying; Yan, Ya; Miao, Mao; Zhan, Ke; Li, Pingwei; Yang, Junhe; Zhao, Bin; Xia, Bao Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-purity hydrogen produced by water splitting is considered as one of the most promising fuels to replace traditional fossil fuels.  Developing highly efficient electrocatalysts toward H evolution is vital for the realization of large-scale H generation.  Glycerol is used here in a facile solvothermal process to synthesize edge-rich ultrathin MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) composites.  The introduction of glycerol plays an important role in the formation of such interesting structures.  The MoS2/RGO electrocatalyst exhibits excellent H evolution reaction (HER) activity and remarkable stability, owing to the rich active edges and improved elec. cond. of the catalyst composites.  This work provides new insights to engineer the structures of MoSx-based composites and thus achieves more active and efficient electrocatalysts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjjlLnyLvFnrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj7Mk0sVp_T-w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhslGltr%252FE&amp;md5=14a87df6c827823e935b4369194ce529</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2008.09.045"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Velamakanni, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bozoklu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stoller, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Piner, R.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Several nanometer-thick graphene oxide films deposited on silicon nitride-on silicon substrates were exposed to nine different heat treatments (three in Argon, three in Argon and Hydrogen, and three in ultra-high vacuum), and also a film was held at 70 °C while being exposed to a vapor from hydrazine monohydrate.                         cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Interconnected MoS2 with Enlarged Interlayer Spacing Grown on Carbon Nanofibers as a Flexible Anode Toward Superior Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei; Bi, Ran; Liu, Guoxue; Tian, Yaxi; Zhang, Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) has attracted extensive research interest as a fascinating anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of its high specific capacity of 670 mA h g-1.  However, unsatisfied cycling durability and poor rate performance are two barriers that hinder MoS2 for practical application in SIBs.  Herein, 3D interconnected MoS2 with enlarged interlayer spacing epitaxially grown on 1D electrospinning carbon nanofibers (denoted as MoS2@CNFs) was prepd. as a flexible anode for SIBs via L-cysteine-assisted hydrothermal method. The elaborate strategy developed in this work opens a new avenue to prep. highly improved energy storage materials, esp. suitable for flexible electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpKvgYWiMwJC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj9Tfh4axheCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtlyktLjP&amp;md5=a0c8d21f6ae706ef3ae9540d932bf1ad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402428"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, S.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D MoS2-Graphene Microspheres Consisting of Multiple Nanospheres with Superior Sodium Ion Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Choi, Seung Ho; Ko, You Na; Lee, Jung-Kul; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1780-1788</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.  The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.  The outstanding Na ion storage properties of the 3D MoS2-graphene composite microspheres may be attributed to the reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers and to the 3D structure of the porous graphene microspheres.  The reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers relaxes the strain and lowers the barrier for Na+ insertion.  The empty nanospheres of the graphene offer voids for vol. expansion and pathways for fast electron transfer during repeated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MXJGPkuEhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj9Tfh4axheCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvVSitbk%253D&amp;md5=18c752a0885c5236fc4aefe504f5d301</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref56'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA05714K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sheng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive Behaviours of Na<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>@CNT Coaxial Nanocables for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive behaviours of Na2Ti3O7@CNT coaxial nanocables for high-performance sodium-ion capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Shengyang; Shen, Laifa; Li, Hongsen; Nie, Ping; Zhu, Yaoyao; Sheng, Qi; Zhang, Xiaogang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid sodium-ion capacitors (NICs) have tremendous potential in large-scale energy storage applications due to their low cost, long lifetime and high power.  However, it remains a great challenge to find a desirable anode material with fast kinetics and superior cycle life.  Here an applicable strategy to in situ grow Na2Ti3O7 on 1D CNTs as an anode material for sodium-ion capacitors is presented.  Benefiting from the unique 1D nanostructure and the presence of pseudocapacitive charge storage mechanism, the Na2Ti3O7@CNT electrode exhibits excellent electrochem. performance with high rate capability and superb cycling stability.  Moreover, a high performance hybrid NIC is also fabricated by using Na2Ti3O7@CNTs as an anode and activated carbon derived from the outer peanut shell as a cathode, which delivers high energy d. (58.5 W h kg-1), high power d. (3000 W kg-1), and long term cycle life (retaining ca. 75% of its original capacity at 0.4 A g-1 after 4000 cycles).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGovs0Jr2Mx5ibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj9Tfh4axheCg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVygtr%252FL&amp;md5=942921c8dff713d4d077a8e205054160</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref57'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201706652"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancing sodium-ion battery performance with interlayer-expanded MoS2-PEO nanocomposites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yifei; Liang, Yanliang; Robles Hernandez, Francisco C.; Deog Yoo, Hyun; An, Qinyou; Yao, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">453-461</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The larger ionic radius of Na ion (1.06 Å) compared with that of Li ion (0.76 Å) is a fundamental reason for the inferior diffusion kinetics of Na ion in intercalation hosts.  Here we report interlayer expansion of intercalation hosts as a general strategy to facilitate the solid-state diffusion of Na ions.  Based on this strategy, poly(ethylene oxide)-intercalated MoS2 composites (PEO-MoS2) were synthesized via a facile exfoliation-restacking method and tested as anode materials for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  The interlayer spacing of MoS2 was increased from 0.615 nm to 1.45 nm by insertion of controlled amts. of PEO.  The bilayer PEO-intercalated MoS2 composite (PEO2L-MoS2) exhibits a specific capacity of 225 mA h g-1 under a c.d. of 50 mA g-1, twice as high as that of com. MoS2 (com-MoS2), and shows improved rate performance due to enhanced Na-ion diffusivity.  The improvement in the electrochem. performance demonstrates that interlayer expansion is an effective strategy for the development of high performance electrode materials for battery technologies based on the storage of large ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPDeJY5F5U6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilIdOn_Ugphg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXptFGhu7w%253D&amp;md5=2ff5dbb1e1ec86fba37e45f24a07c7f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref59'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201703252"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.                         cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitance-boosted ultrafast Na storage in a pie-like FeS@C nanohybrid as an advanced anode material for sodium-ion full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Bao-Hua; Wang, Ying-Ying; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Ning, Qiu-Li; Xi, Xiao-Tong; Pang, Wei-Lin; Cao, An-Min; Wang, Xinlong; Zhang, Jing-Ping; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9218-9225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In order to develop promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a novel pie-like FeS@C (P-FeS@C) nanohybrid, in which all ultrasmall FeS nanocrystals (NCs) are completely embedded into the carbon network and sealed by a protective carbon shell, has been prepd.  The unique pie-like structure can effectively speed up the kinetics of electrode reactions, while the carbon shell stabilizes the FeS NCs inside.  Studies show that the electrochem. reaction processes of P-FeS@C electrodes are dominated by the pseudocapacitive behavior, leading to an ultrafast Na+-insertion/extn. reaction.  Hence, the prepd. P-FeS@C nanohybrid exhibits superior Na-storage properties esp. high rate capability in half cells.  For example, it can deliver reversible capacities of 555.1 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 over 150 cycles and about 60.4 mA h g-1 at 80 A g-1 (an ultrahigh c.d. even higher than that of the capacitor test).  Furthermore, an advanced P-FeS@C//Na3V2(PO4)2O2F full cell has been assembled out, which delivers a stable specific capacity of 441.2 mA h g-1 after 80 cycles at 0.5 A g-1 with a capacity retention of 91.8%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGonBrKimr3tJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lilIdOn_Ugphg"> &gt;&gt;
